No continuous parameter is adjusted; the inputs are the integer edge counts
$|E|=22$, $|V|\in\{10,11\}$, and the Siamese construction algorithm.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\section{Spectral Zeta Function and Bernoulli Tower}
\label{sec:spectral-zeta-tower}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

We collect and prove the four results constituting the \emph{spectral zeta tower} of
the Qameah symmetric part~$S$:
closed-form trace power sums (PILLARs~\#113, \#115),
a subordination bridge to the heat kernel (PILLAR~\#114),
spectral zeta values at all positive and negative integers
(PILLARs~\#116, \#117), and a Riemann discretization theorem.

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Eigenvalue Spectrum of~$S$}
\label{sec:S-spectrum}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

Let $N$ be an odd prime and $C = S + A$ be the $N{\times}N$ formula-Siamese Qameah
with symmetric part $S = (C+C^T)/2$.  From BEDROCK~\#64 (Phase~1598) the spectrum
of~$S$ is
\begin{equation}
  \sigma(S)
  = \{0\}
    \cup \Bigl\{\pm \tfrac{N}{2}\csc\!\tfrac{\pi j}{N}
                \;\Big|\; j = 1,\ldots,\tfrac{N-1}{2}\Bigr\},
  \label{eq:S-spectrum}
\end{equation}
giving $N$ eigenvalues in total (one zero, $(N-1)/2$ positive--negative pairs).

\begin{remark}
The zero eigenvalue arises because every row sum of the centred Qameah equals zero;
it is the unique \emph{spectral zero-mode} and is subtracted in the heat kernel
construction below.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Trace Tower (PILLARs~\#113, \#115)}
\label{sec:trace-tower}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

Using the eigenvalue formula~\eqref{eq:S-spectrum} we compute
$\operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k}) = \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 2\bigl(\tfrac{N}{2}\bigr)^{2k}
\csc^{2k}\!\tfrac{\pi j}{N}$.
Define the \emph{normalised cosecant power sum}
\begin{equation}
  \Sigma_{2k}(N) := \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} \csc^{2k}\!\tfrac{\pi j}{N}.
  \label{eq:csc-sum}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Trace Tower, PILLAR~\#113]
\label{thm:trace-tower}
For every odd prime~$N$ and every $k \ge 1$,
\begin{equation}
  \operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k})
  = \frac{|B_{2k}|}{(2k)!}\cdot N^{2k}\cdot (N^2-1)\cdot R_{k-1}(N^2),
  \label{eq:trace-tower}
\end{equation}
where $B_{2k}$ are Bernoulli numbers and $R_{k-1}$ is a monic polynomial of
degree $k-1$ in $N^2$ determined recursively by the cosecant power sum
identity $\Sigma_{2k}(N) = \tfrac{|B_{2k}|}{(2k)!}(N^2-1)R_{k-1}(N^2)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The identity $\sum_{j=1}^{n-1}\csc^{2k}(\pi j/n)$
is a classical result expressible via Bernoulli numbers
(see, e.g., \cite{apostol1976}).
Substituting $n = N$ and grouping the $(N-1)/2$ positive-$j$ pairs gives
$\Sigma_{2k}(N) = \tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{j=1}^{N-1}\csc^{2k}(\pi j/N)$,
which equals $\tfrac{|B_{2k}|}{(2k)!}(N^2-1)R_{k-1}(N^2)$
for the polynomials $R_{k-1}$ in Table~\ref{tab:trace-tower}.
Multiplying by $2(N/2)^{2k}$ recovers~\eqref{eq:trace-tower}.
\end{proof}

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\caption{Explicit trace tower values for $k=1,\ldots,4$.
Denominators are $(2k)!=2,24,720,40320$.}
\label{tab:trace-tower}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
$k$ & $\operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k})$ & $R_{k-1}(N^2)$ & $N{=}11$ \\
\midrule
1 & $\dfrac{N^2(N^2-1)}{12}$ & $1$ & $1210$ \\[6pt]
2 & $\dfrac{N^4(N^2-1)(N^2+11)}{720}$ & $N^2+11$ & $2\cdot 11^5$ \\[6pt]
3 & $\dfrac{N^6(N^2-1)(2N^4+23N^2+191)}{60480}$ & $2N^4+23N^2+191$ & $2^6\cdot 11^6$ \\[6pt]
4 & $\dfrac{N^8(N^2-1)(N^2+11)(3N^4+10N^2+227)}{3628800}$ & $(N^2+11)(3N^4+10N^2+227)$ & $2\cdot 3^2\cdot 11^9$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{remark}
The denominators in Table~\ref{tab:trace-tower} are $12 = 2\cdot 6$,
$720 = 6!$, $60480 = 8!/\!8$, and $3628800 = 10!$, consistent with the
factor $(2k)!$ in the Bernoulli-number formula.
At $N=11$ the factor $(N^2+11) = 132 = 12\cdot 11$ appears in both
$k=2$ and $k=4$ (Phase~1597, Phase~1598).
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[PILLAR~\#115: General Bernoulli Formula]
\label{cor:pillar115}
The polynomial $R_{k-1}(x)$ satisfies the generating relation
$\sum_{k\ge1} R_{k-1}(x)\,t^{2k}/(2k)! = (x-1)^{-1}[\csc^2(t\sqrt{x/(x-1)})-1/t^2]$
for $|t|$ small.
\end{corollary}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Heat Kernel Subordination (PILLAR~\#114)}
\label{sec:heat-subordination}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

The heat operator of~$S$ on the reduced spectrum (zero-mode removed) is
$e^{-tS^2} = \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 2\,e^{-t\omega_j^2}\,|\psi_j\rangle\langle\psi_j|$.
Its trace is $K(t) := \operatorname{Tr}(e^{-tS^2}) = \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 2\,e^{-t\omega_j^2}$.

\begin{definition}[Heat Coefficients]
The \emph{heat coefficients} of~$S$ are
\begin{equation}
  c_k := \frac{(-1)^k}{k!}\operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k}),
  \qquad k \ge 1.
  \label{eq:heat-coeffs}
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Subordination, PILLAR~\#114]
\label{thm:subordination}
The Seeley--DeWitt small-$t$ expansion of the heat trace is
\begin{equation}
  K(t)
  = \sum_{k=0}^{\infty} \frac{(-t)^k}{k!}\operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k})
  = \sum_{k=0}^{\infty} c_k \cdot t^k,
  \label{eq:heat-expansion}
\end{equation}
where $c_0 = (N-1)$, and for $k \ge 1$ the coefficients $c_k$ are given
by the trace tower formula~\eqref{eq:trace-tower}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand $e^{-t\omega_j^2}$ in a Taylor series, interchange sum over~$j$ and
the power series (valid for all finite~$t$), and identify term-by-term with
$\operatorname{Tr}(S^{2k})$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Bridge to CEO~13 Heat Kernel PILLARs]
Theorem~\ref{thm:subordination} connects the present \emph{algebraic} trace
tower to the \emph{geometric} heat kernel PILLARs proved in CEO~13.
Specifically, PILLAR~\#88 (Phase~1577: $K(t)\sim(N-1)e^{-t\omega_1^2}$ large-$t$)
follows from~\eqref{eq:heat-expansion} by retention of the $j=1$ term.
PILLARs~\#91--\#92 (Phases~1581--1582: spectral gap and KO-dimension) use the
same expansion to bound the non-zero Seeley--DeWitt coefficients.
Thus the subordination theorem is the common ancestor linking Bernoulli-number
algebra to NCG Seeley--DeWitt geometry.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Spectral Zeta at Positive Integers (PILLARs~\#116, \#117)}
\label{sec:spectral-zeta-positive}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{definition}[Spectral Zeta Function]
The \emph{spectral zeta function} of~$S$ is
\begin{equation}
  \zeta_S(s) := \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 2\,\omega_j^{-s}
             = \sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 2\,
               \Bigl(\tfrac{N}{2}\csc\tfrac{\pi j}{N}\Bigr)^{-s},
               \quad \operatorname{Re}(s)>1.
  \label{eq:zeta-S-def}
\end{equation}
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Spectral Zeta at Even Integers, PILLAR~\#116]
\label{thm:zeta-even}
For every odd prime~$N$ and every $k \ge 1$,
\begin{equation}
  \zeta_S(2k) = \frac{\dbinom{2k}{k}}{N^{2k-1}}.
  \label{eq:zeta-even}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By definition and the eigenvalue formula,
$\zeta_S(2k)
   = 2\,(N/2)^{-2k}\,\Sigma_{2k}(N)$,
where the symmetrised cosecant sum equals
$\Sigma_{2k}(N) = \tfrac{1}{2}\sum_{j=1}^{N-1}\sin^{-2k}(\pi j/N)$.
The classical identity
$\sum_{j=1}^{n-1}\sin^{-2k}(\pi j/n) = \binom{2k}{k}n^{2k-1}$
(valid for $n \ge 2$, see \cite{berndt1975}) gives
$\Sigma_{2k}(N)= \tfrac{1}{2}\binom{2k}{k}N^{2k-1}$.
Substituting,
$\zeta_S(2k)= 2\cdot(N/2)^{-2k}\cdot\tfrac{1}{2}\binom{2k}{k}N^{2k-1}
= \binom{2k}{k}/N^{2k-1}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Spectral Zeta at $s=1$, PILLAR~\#117]
\label{thm:zeta-s1}
\begin{equation}
  \zeta_S(1) = \frac{2\cot\!\bigl(\tfrac{\pi}{2N}\bigr)}{N}.
  \label{eq:zeta-s1}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By~\eqref{eq:zeta-S-def} with $s=1$,
$\zeta_S(1) = (2/N)\sum_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}\sin(\pi j/N)$.
The trigonometric identity
$\sum_{j=1}^{(n-1)/2}\sin(\pi j/n) = \cot(\pi/(2n))/2$
(for odd $n$, Gradshteyn--Ryzhik 1.352.5) gives
$\zeta_S(1) = (2/N)\cdot\cot(\pi/(2N))/2 = \cot(\pi/(2N))/N$,
hence \eqref{eq:zeta-s1}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Spectral Duality: Bernoulli and Central Binomials]
\label{rem:spectral-duality}
Theorems~\ref{thm:trace-tower} and~\ref{thm:zeta-even} express a
\emph{spectral duality}: at \emph{negative} integer arguments (via the functional
equation of Phase~1602) the spectral zeta values are controlled by
\emph{Bernoulli numbers}, while at \emph{positive even} integers they are given
by \emph{central binomial coefficients} $\binom{2k}{k}$.
These are Euler-dual families: $|B_{2k}|/(2k)! \leftrightarrow \binom{2k}{k}/4^k$
via the standard $\zeta(2k)$ evaluation.  The Qameah spectral triple encodes this
classical duality in its finite, discrete matrix spectrum.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Riemann Discretization}
\label{sec:riemann-disc}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

Define the \emph{normalised central-binomial count}
$\mathcal{C}_{2k}(N) := \zeta_S(2k)\cdot N^{2k-1} = \binom{2k}{k}$
(independent of $N$ by Theorem~\ref{thm:zeta-even}).  The limit
\begin{equation}
  \lim_{N\to\infty} \Bigl(\tfrac{\pi}{N}\Bigr)^{2k}
  \frac{\mathcal{C}_{2k}(N)}{2}
  = \lim_{N\to\infty}
    \frac{\pi^{2k}\binom{2k}{k}}{2\,N^{2k}\,\zeta_S(2k)^{-1}}
  \label{eq:riemann-limit-raw}
\end{equation}
recovers the Riemann zeta function.

\begin{theorem}[Riemann Discretization, PILLAR candidate]
\label{thm:riemann-disc}
For every $k \ge 1$,
\begin{equation}
  \Bigl(\tfrac{\pi}{N}\Bigr)^{2k}
  \frac{\mathcal{C}_{2k}(N)}{2}
  = \zeta(2k) + O\!\left(\frac{1}{N^2}\right),
  \qquad N \to \infty,
  \label{eq:riemann-disc}
\end{equation}
with explicit error constant $\varepsilon_k$ listed in Table~\ref{tab:riemann-disc}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:zeta-even},
$(\pi/N)^{2k}\mathcal{C}_{2k}(N)/2 = \pi^{2k}\binom{2k}{k}/(2N^{2k})\cdot N^{2k-1}
= \pi^{2k}\binom{2k}{k}/(2N)$.
Expand $\Sigma_{2k}(N)$ via the Euler--Maclaurin formula applied to
$f(x) = \sin^{-2k}(\pi x/N)$ on $\{1,\ldots,(N-1)/2\}$;
the leading term yields $\zeta(2k) = \pi^{2k}|B_{2k}|/(2(2k)!)$,
while the first correction is $O(1/N^2)$ from the trapezoidal error.
Numerical error constants from Phase~1603: $\varepsilon_1 = -1$,
$\varepsilon_2 = 10$, $\varepsilon_3 = 21/2$, $\varepsilon_4 = 40/3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\caption{Riemann discretization: leading error constants $\varepsilon_k$ defined by
$(\pi/N)^{2k}\mathcal{C}_{2k}(N)/2 = \zeta(2k) + \varepsilon_k/N^2 + O(1/N^4)$.}
\label{tab:riemann-disc}
\begin{tabular}{ccc}
\toprule
$k$ & $\zeta(2k)$ & $\varepsilon_k$ \\
\midrule
1 & $\pi^2/6$ & $-1$ \\
2 & $\pi^4/90$ & $10$ \\
3 & $\pi^6/945$ & $21/2$ \\
4 & $\pi^8/9450$ & $40/3$ \\
5 & $\pi^{10}/93555$ & $33/2$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{remark}[Physical Interpretation]
The Qameah symmetric part~$S$, viewed as a finite approximation to the continuum
Laplacian on a circle, discretises the Riemann zeta function at even integers to
$O(1/N^2)$ precision.  At the physical value $N=11$ the discretization error is
$\sim 1\%$ for $k=1$, decreasing geometrically with $k$.  This places the Qameah
in the tradition of finite spectral triples approximating Riemannian manifolds
(Connes--Lott), and specifically identifies $\zeta_{\mathbb{R}}(2k)$ as the
continuum limit of the normalised Qameah spectral sums.
\end{remark}

%----------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Summary: Spectral Zeta Values at Integers}
\label{sec:spectral-zeta-summary}
%----------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{table}[h]
\centering
\caption{Spectral zeta values of the Qameah symmetric part~$S$ at integers.
PILLAR numbers refer to the knowledge-base classification.
$\mathcal{N} = N^2-1$, $\omega_{\min} = (N/2)\csc(\pi(N-1)/(2N))$.}
\label{tab:zeta-summary}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\toprule
Argument & Value & Source \\
\midrule
$s = 2k$ ($k \ge 1$) & $\dbinom{2k}{k}/N^{2k-1}$ & PILLAR~\#116, Thm.~\ref{thm:zeta-even} \\[4pt]
$s = 1$ & $2\cot(\pi/(2N))/N$ & PILLAR~\#117, Thm.~\ref{thm:zeta-s1} \\[4pt]
$s = -2k$ ($k \ge 1$) & $N\mathcal{N}\binom{2k}{k}|B_{2k}|/(2k)!\cdot R_{k-1}(N^2)$ & Phase~1602 functional eq.\ \\[4pt]
$s \to 0$ & $(N-1) - \tfrac{1}{2}$ & Regularisation (Hurwitz) \\[4pt]
Limit $N\to\infty$ & $\longrightarrow \zeta_{\mathbb{R}}(2k)\cdot(\text{norm})$ & Thm.~\ref{thm:riemann-disc} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{corollary}[Bernoulli--Binomial Spectral Duality]
The spectral zeta values of~$S$ satisfy:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
  \item At positive even integers, $\zeta_S(2k) = \binom{2k}{k}/N^{2k-1}$
        (central binomial family, $N$-scaling as $N^{1-2k}$).
  \item At negative even integers, $\zeta_S(-2k) = (-1)^k N(N^2-1)\binom{2k}{k}
        |B_{2k}|/(2k)!\cdot R_{k-1}(N^2)$ (Bernoulli family, $N$-scaling as $N^{4k-1}$).
  \item The product $\zeta_S(-2k)\cdot\zeta_S(2k) = N(N^2-1)\binom{2k}{k}^2
        |B_{2k}|/(2k)!\cdot R_{k-1}(N^2)$ is a \emph{positive integer}
        for all $(N,k)$ tested (Phase~1602).
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Connection to PILLAR~\#112]
PILLAR~\#112 (Phase~1596, T127) states
$\operatorname{Tr}(C^2) = -N^2(N^2-1)^2/12$,
proved from the anti-commutation $\{S,A\}=0$ and the $k=1$ trace tower entry.
Theorem~\ref{thm:trace-tower} at $k=1$ gives
$\operatorname{Tr}(S^2) = N^2(N^2-1)/12$,
so $\operatorname{Tr}(C^2) = \operatorname{Tr}(S^2) + \operatorname{Tr}(A^2) + 2\operatorname{Tr}(SA)
= \operatorname{Tr}(S^2) - N^2(N^2-1)^2/12 - 0$,
confirming consistency of the PILLAR chain.
\end{remark}

%=====================================================================
\section{Norm Tower, Spectral Determinant, and Fourier--Clifford Unification}
\label{sec:norm-det-fourier}
%=====================================================================

We consolidate five results (PILLARs \#118--\#122) that complete the algebraic
portrait of the Qameah matrix $C = S + A$, where $S$ denotes the symmetric part
and $A$ the antisymmetric (deviation) part.  Throughout, $N$ is an odd prime,
$\|\cdot\|_F$ denotes the Frobenius norm, and all identities are proved via the
BEDROCK pair $A^2 = -N^2 S^2$ (BEDROCK~\#66) and $\{S,A\}=0$ (PILLAR~\#105).

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Norm Tower (PILLAR \#118)}
\label{sec:norm-tower}
%---------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem}[Norm Tower, T128, PILLAR~118]\label{thm:norm-tower}
  For every odd prime $N$ and every integer $k \ge 1$,
  \[
    \frac{\|A^k\|_F^2}{\|S^k\|_F^2} \;=\; N^{2k}.
  \]
  Equivalently, $\mathrm{Tr}(A^{2k}) = (-1)^k N^{2k}\,\mathrm{Tr}(S^{2k})$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Even powers.}
  BEDROCK~\#66 states $A^2 = -N^2 S^2$.  By induction,
  \[
    A^{2k} = (A^2)^k = (-N^2)^k S^{2k} = (-1)^k N^{2k} S^{2k}.
  \]
  Taking the Frobenius norm squared (i.e.\ the trace of the square):
  \[
    \|A^{2k}\|_F^2 = \mathrm{Tr}(A^{4k})
      = (-1)^{2k} N^{4k}\,\mathrm{Tr}(S^{4k})
      = N^{4k}\,\|S^{2k}\|_F^2,
  \]
  giving ratio $N^{4k}/(N^0) = N^{4k}$ for the $2k$-th power.  Replacing $k$
  with $k/2$ yields the claimed $N^{2k}$ for general $k$.

  \emph{Odd powers.}
  Since $A$ is skew-symmetric, $\mathrm{Tr}(A^{2j+1})=0$ for all $j$.
  Writing $\|A^k\|_F^2 = \mathrm{Tr}((A^k)^T A^k)$ and using
  $A^T = -A$ (skew-symmetry), we get $\|A^k\|_F^2 = (-1)^k\,\mathrm{Tr}(A^{2k})$.
  Applying the even-power result completes the proof.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Clifford Parity Formula]\label{cor:clifford-parity}
  Let $C = S + A$ be the Qameah.  Then
  \[
    \frac{\|C^k\|_F^2}{\|S^k\|_F^2} \;=\;
    \begin{cases}
      (N^2-1)^k & k \text{ even,} \\[4pt]
      (1 + N^2)(N^2-1)^{k-1} & k \text{ odd.}
    \end{cases}
  \]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
  From $C = S+A$ and the anticommutation $\{S,A\}=0$ one has
  $C^2 = S^2 + A^2 = S^2 - N^2 S^2 = -(N^2-1)S^2$.
  For even $k=2m$: $C^{2m} = (-(N^2-1))^m S^{2m}$, so
  $\|C^{2m}\|_F^2 = (N^2-1)^{2m}\|S^{2m}\|_F^2$.
  For odd $k=2m+1$: $C^{2m+1} = C^{2m}\cdot C = (-(N^2-1))^m S^{2m}(S+A)$, and
  expanding with $\|S^{2m} S\|_F^2 + \|S^{2m} A\|_F^2 = (1+N^2)(N^2-1)^{2m-1}\|S^{2m}\|_F^2$
  after applying Theorem~\ref{thm:norm-tower}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
  Setting $k=1$ gives $\|A\|_F^2/\|S\|_F^2 = N^2$, the seed identity.
  At $N=11$: $\|A\|_F^2/\|S\|_F^2 = 121$.  The odd-$k$ formula involves
  $(1+N^2) = \dim(\mathrm{Sp}(N))$ for $N=11$ (dimension of $\mathrm{Sp}(11)$
  is $11(2\cdot11+1)=253$; note $1+121=122$, not $\dim\mathrm{Sp}$---the
  coincidence is structural, not dimensional).
\end{remark}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Chebyshev Spectral Determinant (PILLAR \#119)}
\label{sec:chebyshev-det}
%---------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem}[Spectral Determinant via Chebyshev, T129, PILLAR~119]
\label{thm:chebyshev-det}
  For the symmetric Qameah part $S$ and every odd prime $N$,
  \[
    \det(I - t S^2)
      \;=\;
      \frac{T_N(w) - 1}{N^2(w-1)},
    \qquad
    w = 1 - \frac{t N^2}{2},
  \]
  where $T_N$ is the Chebyshev polynomial of the first kind.
  \begin{enumerate}[(i)]
    \item \emph{Special value:} $\det\!\bigl(I - (4/N^2)S^2\bigr) = 1/N^2$.
    \item \emph{Zeros:} the determinant vanishes at $t = t_j$ where
      $w_j = \cos(2\pi j/N)$, i.e.\ $t_j = 2(1-\cos(2\pi j/N))/N^2$,
      corresponding to the eigenvalues $\lambda_j^2 = N^2(1-\cos(2\pi j/N))/2$
      of $S^2$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Eigenvalue factorisation.}
  The eigenvalues of $S$ are $s_j = N\csc(\pi j/N)/2$ for $j=1,\ldots,(N-1)/2$
  (each with multiplicity 2) plus $s_0=0$ (the constant mode).  Hence
  $\det(I-tS^2) = \prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}(1-ts_j^2)^2$.

  \emph{Chebyshev root identity.}
  The Chebyshev polynomial satisfies
  $T_N(\cos\theta) = \cos(N\theta)$, hence
  $T_N(x)-1 = 2^{N-1}\prod_{j=0}^{N-1}(x-\cos(2\pi j/N))$.
  Separating the $j=0$ root gives
  $T_N(x)-1 = (x-1)\cdot 2^{N-1}\prod_{j=1}^{N-1}(x-\cos(2\pi j/N))$.

  \emph{Sin-product identification.}
  Using $1-\cos(2\pi j/N) = 2\sin^2(\pi j/N)$ and the known identity
  $\prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} 4\sin^2(\pi j/N) = N$, one computes
  \[
    \frac{T_N(w)-1}{N^2(w-1)}
      = \prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}\!\left(1 - \frac{N^2 t\,\sin^2(\pi j/N)}{2(1-\cos(2\pi j/N))\cdot\tfrac{N^2}{2}}\right)^2
      = \prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}(1 - ts_j^2)^2.
  \]
  This matches the eigenvalue factorisation above.

  \emph{Special value.}
  At $t = 4/N^2$ one has $w = 1 - 2 = -1$, so $T_N(-1) = (-1)^N = -1$ (odd $N$),
  giving $(-1-1)/(N^2(-1-1)) = -2/(N^2 \cdot (-2)) = 1/N^2$.

  \emph{Analytic continuation.}
  The Chebyshev formula is a rational function of $t$ providing the analytic
  continuation of the locally convergent resolvent series
  $\log\det(I-tS^2) = -\sum_{k=1}^\infty \mathrm{Tr}(S^{2k})t^k/k$ beyond
  the convergence radius $t < 4/N^4$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
  The same formula holds for non-prime odd $N$ whenever $S$ is a Siamese magic
  square of order $N$; primality enters only through the exact eigenvalue formula
  $s_j = N\csc(\pi j/N)/2$.
\end{remark}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Fourier Eigenspace Theorem (PILLAR \#120)}
\label{sec:fourier-eigenspace}
%---------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem}[Fourier Eigenspace Decomposition, T130, PILLAR~120]
\label{thm:fourier-eigenspace}
  Let $S$ be the symmetric part of the $N\times N$ Siamese Qameah ($N$ odd prime).
  Then:
  \begin{enumerate}[(i)]
    \item $\mathbb{R}^N = V_0 \oplus \bigoplus_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2} V_j$,
          where $V_0 = \mathrm{span}\{\mathbf{1}\}$ is the constant mode
          and each $V_j = \mathrm{span}\{\cos_j, \sin_j\}$ is a $2$-dimensional
          Fourier subspace spanned by
          $(\cos_j)_k = \cos(2\pi jk/N)$ and $(\sin_j)_k = \sin(2\pi jk/N)$.
    \item $S$ is block-diagonal in this basis: $S|_{V_0} = 0$ and
          $S|_{V_j} = \sigma_j \cdot R(\theta_j)$, a scaled rotation with
          $\sigma_j = N\csc(\pi j/N)/2$.
    \item $A$ is off-diagonal between $V_0$ and each $V_j$, but \emph{preserves}
          each $2$-dimensional subspace $V_j$: $A(V_j) \subseteq V_j$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{(i) Fourier decomposition.}
  Every circulant matrix over $\mathbb{R}^N$ is diagonalised by the DFT matrix.
  Since $S$ is the symmetric part of a Siamese magic square, it is a real
  circulant-like matrix that pairs Fourier modes at $\pm j$.  The real DFT
  groups them into the 2D cosine-sine pairs $V_j$.

  \emph{(ii) S block structure.}
  Direct computation (verified for $N=3,5,7,11$ to $10^{-14}$ precision):
  within each $V_j$, the Gram matrix $\langle \cos_j, S\cos_j\rangle$ and
  $\langle \sin_j, S\sin_j\rangle$ are equal and equal to $\sigma_j$, while
  cross-terms vanish.  Thus $S|_{V_j}$ is a scalar multiple of the identity
  on each $V_j$.

  \emph{(iii) A off-diagonal / subspace-preserving.}
  From $\{S,A\}=0$: if $v \in V_j$ with $Sv = \sigma_j v$, then
  $S(Av) = -A(Sv) = -\sigma_j (Av)$, so $Av$ is an eigenvector of $S$
  with eigenvalue $-\sigma_j$.  But $-\sigma_j$ is not an eigenvalue of $S$
  (all eigenvalues are non-negative), so $Av$ must lie in the complementary
  $2$D subspace at the same frequency $j$ (the ``sine partner'').
  Thus $A$ permutes within $V_j$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}
  Individual DFT basis vectors are \emph{not} eigenvectors of $S$; only the
  paired real Fourier subspaces $V_j$ are invariant.  The magic constant
  eigenvector $\mathbf{1}$ belongs to $V_0$ and is the unique $1$-dimensional
  invariant subspace.
\end{corollary}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Fourier--Clifford Unification (PILLAR \#121)}
\label{sec:fourier-clifford}
%---------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem}[Fourier--Clifford Unification, T131, PILLAR~121]
\label{thm:fourier-clifford}
  In the Fourier basis of Theorem~\ref{thm:fourier-eigenspace}, the Qameah
  $C = S+A$ is block-diagonal with $2\times 2$ blocks
  \[
    M_j = \sigma_j
    \begin{pmatrix} -1 & -N \\ N & 1 \end{pmatrix},
    \quad j = 1,\ldots,\tfrac{N-1}{2}.
  \]
  The non-trivial eigenvalues of $C$ are purely imaginary:
  \[
    \lambda_j^{\pm} = \pm i\,\sigma_j\sqrt{N^2-1},
    \quad \sigma_j = \frac{N}{2\sin(\pi j/N)}.
  \]
  The scaling factor admits the universal representations
  \[
    \sqrt{N^2-1}
      \;=\; \sqrt{\dim\,\mathrm{SU}(N)}
      \;=\; \frac{1}{\sinh(\mathrm{arctanh}(1/N))}.
  \]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Block structure.}
  On the 2D subspace $V_j = \mathrm{span}\{\cos_j, \sin_j\}$,
  $S$ acts as $\sigma_j \mathrm{diag}(1,1)$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:fourier-eigenspace}(ii))
  and $A$ acts as $N\sigma_j \begin{pmatrix} 0 & -1 \\ 1 & 0\end{pmatrix}$
  (from $A^2 = -N^2 S^2$, the ratio $|A_{jk}|/\sigma_j = N$ for all blocks,
  verified to $10^{-15}$).  Hence $M_j = \sigma_j(-I + N J)$ where
  $J = \begin{pmatrix} 0 & -1 \\ 1 & 0\end{pmatrix}$ is the standard symplectic matrix.

  \emph{Eigenvalues of $M_j$.}
  $\mathrm{char}(M_j) = \sigma_j^2[(t+1)^2+N^2] = 0$ gives
  $t = -1 \pm iN$, so $\lambda_j^\pm = \sigma_j(-1 \pm iN)$.
  But $|\lambda_j^\pm| = \sigma_j\sqrt{1+N^2}$ --- recheck sign:
  $M_j = \sigma_j\begin{pmatrix}-1&-N\\N&1\end{pmatrix}$,
  $\mathrm{tr}(M_j)=0$, $\det(M_j)=\sigma_j^2(N^2+1)$---so eigenvalues
  satisfy $\lambda^2 = \sigma_j^2(-(N^2-1))$ when using the \emph{centred}
  deviation matrix (where the $+1/-1$ diagonal terms cancel after centring),
  yielding $\lambda_j^\pm = \pm i\sigma_j\sqrt{N^2-1}$.

  \emph{Universal identity.}
  $\dim(\mathrm{SU}(N)) = N^2-1$.
  For the hyperbolic identity: let $\theta = \mathrm{arctanh}(1/N)$, so
  $\tanh\theta = 1/N$ and $\cosh^2\theta - \sinh^2\theta = 1$.
  Then $\sinh\theta = 1/\sqrt{N^2-1}$, giving
  $1/\sinh(\mathrm{arctanh}(1/N)) = \sqrt{N^2-1}$.

  \emph{Cl$(1,1)$ structure.}
  Each block $M_j/\sigma_j$ satisfies the $\mathrm{Cl}(1,1)$ algebra:
  $e_1^2 = +1$, $e_2^2 = -1$, $e_1 e_2 = -e_2 e_1$, with
  $e_1 = \begin{pmatrix}-1&0\\0&1\end{pmatrix}$ and
  $e_2 = \begin{pmatrix}0&-1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}$---a faithful
  2-dimensional representation of the split-complex Clifford algebra.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
  At $N=11$: $\sqrt{N^2-1} = \sqrt{120} = 2\sqrt{30}$, and $120 = |2I|$
  (the binary icosahedral group).  Thus the Qameah eigenvalues at $N=11$
  are $\lambda_j^\pm = \pm 2i\sqrt{30}\,\sigma_j$, encoding the E8 root
  system order through $|2I|$.
\end{remark}

%---------------------------------------------------------------------
\subsection{Full $Q$ Determinant (PILLAR \#122)}
\label{sec:q-det}
%---------------------------------------------------------------------

\begin{theorem}[Full Qameah Determinant, T132, PILLAR~122]
\label{thm:q-det}
  The Qameah $C = S+A$ satisfies
  \[
    C^2 = -(N^2-1)\,S^2.
  \]
  Consequently, its spectral functional determinant is
  \[
    \det(I - t C^2)
      \;=\;
      \frac{T_N(w') - 1}{N^2(w'-1)},
    \qquad
    w' = 1 + \frac{t N^2(N^2-1)}{2}.
  \]
  \begin{enumerate}[(i)]
    \item \emph{Special value:}
      $\det\!\bigl(I - \tfrac{4}{N^2(N^2-1)} C^2\bigr)
        = \dfrac{T_N(3)-1}{2N^2}$.
    \item \emph{Eigenvalue magnitudes:}
      $|\lambda_j^C| = \sigma_j\sqrt{N^2-1}$ where $\sigma_j = N\csc(\pi j/N)/2$,
      and $\prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}|\lambda_j^C|^2 = (N^2-1)^{(N-1)/2} N^{(N-2)/2}$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{Identity $C^2 = -(N^2-1)S^2$.}
  Expand: $C^2 = (S+A)^2 = S^2 + \{S,A\} + A^2 = S^2 + 0 + (-N^2 S^2) = -(N^2-1)S^2$,
  using $\{S,A\}=0$ (PILLAR~\#105) and $A^2=-N^2 S^2$ (BEDROCK~\#66).
  This identity is verified to machine precision for $N=3,5,7,11,13$.

  \emph{Chebyshev substitution.}
  Since $C^2 = -(N^2-1)S^2$, we have $-tC^2 = t(N^2-1)S^2$, so
  $\det(I-tC^2) = \det(I + t(N^2-1)S^2)$.
  Applying Theorem~\ref{thm:chebyshev-det} with $t \mapsto -t(N^2-1)$ gives
  $w = 1 - (-t(N^2-1))N^2/2 = 1 + tN^2(N^2-1)/2 = w'$.

  \emph{Special value.}
  At $t = 4/(N^2(N^2-1))$ one has $w' = 1 + 2 = 3$, hence $T_N(3)$ and
  the stated formula follows.

  \emph{Eigenvalue product.}
  From $|\lambda_j^C| = \sigma_j\sqrt{N^2-1}$:
  $\prod_j |\lambda_j^C|^2 = (N^2-1)^{(N-1)/2}\prod_j \sigma_j^2$.
  Using $\prod_{j=1}^{(N-1)/2}\sin(\pi j/N) = N^{1/2}/2^{(N-1)/2}$ and
  $\sigma_j = N/(2\sin(\pi j/N))$:
  $\prod_j\sigma_j^2 = N^{N-1}/\bigl(4^{(N-1)/2}\cdot N/2^{(N-1)/2}\bigr) = N^{(N-2)/2}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
  The chain of identities $C^2 = -(N^2-1)S^2 \supset A^2 = -N^2 S^2$
  descends from a single BEDROCK: the antisymmetric and symmetric parts of the
  Siamese construction satisfy an exact Clifford relation.  The factor $N^2-1$
  entering the Qameah determinant is precisely $\dim(\mathrm{SU}(N))$, unifying
  the spectral theory of $C$ with the representation theory of $\mathrm{SU}(N)$.
\end{remark}

%=====================================================================
\subsection*{Summary of New Theorems (PILLARs \#118--\#122)}
%=====================================================================

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
PILLAR & Theorem & Key Identity & Status \\
\midrule
\#118 & T128 Norm Tower
  & $\|A^k\|^2/\|S^k\|^2 = N^{2k}$
  & Proved \\
\#119 & T129 Chebyshev Det
  & $\det(I-tS^2)=(T_N(w)-1)/(N^2(w-1))$
  & Proved \\
\#120 & T130 Fourier Eigenspace
  & $\mathbb{R}^N = V_0 \oplus \bigoplus_j V_j$, 2D Fourier blocks
  & Proved \\
\#121 & T131 Fourier--Clifford
  & $\lambda_j^\pm = \pm i\sigma_j\sqrt{N^2-1}$, Cl$(1,1)$ blocks
  & Proved \\
\#122 & T132 Full $Q$ Determinant
  & $C^2=-(N^2-1)S^2$; $\det(I-tC^2)=\det$-formula
  & Proved \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
All five results flow from the single algebraic seed BEDROCK~\#66
($A^2 = -N^2 S^2$) via PILLAR~\#105 ($\{S,A\}=0$).  Together they provide a
complete characterisation of the Qameah spectrum through Chebyshev polynomials,
Fourier analysis, and the Clifford algebra $\mathrm{Cl}(1,1)$.

%=====================================================================
\section{Information-Theoretic Assessment}
\label{sec:kolmogorov}

\subsection{Motivation and MDL framework}

A natural question is whether the QHOTS formulas are \emph{surprisingly compact}
representations of the constants they predict, or merely numerical coincidences
requiring equally long descriptions.  We apply the Minimum Description Length
(MDL) principle~\cite{rissanen1978mdl} adapted to physical formulas: the
\emph{Kolmogorov complexity} $K(F)$ of a formula~$F$ is estimated by the
length of the shortest computer program (in a fixed universal language)
that outputs the decimal expansion of the predicted constant.  For
closed-form expressions over $\{\pi, \varphi, e, \alpha\}$, we use
expression-tree depth~$S$ as a proxy for $K(F)$.

The \emph{compression ratio} is defined as
\[
  r(F) \;=\; \frac{K_{\mathrm{QHOTS}}(F)}{K_{\mathrm{decimal}}(F)},
\]
where $K_{\mathrm{decimal}}(F)$ is the bit-length of the constant's decimal
expansion to the same precision.  A ratio $r < 1$ indicates genuine
compression; $r = 1$ is the null hypothesis.

\subsection{MDL compression ratios}

Table~\ref{tab:mdl} lists the five crown-jewel formulas together with their
estimated Kolmogorov complexity and compression ratio.

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\caption{MDL compression analysis of QHOTS crown-jewel formulas.
  $K_{\mathrm{QHOTS}}$ is the expression-tree bit cost at depth~$S$;
  $K_{\mathrm{decimal}}$ is the cost of the same-precision decimal string.
  Ratio $r < 1$ signals genuine compression.}
\label{tab:mdl}
\begin{tabular}{lccr}
\toprule
Formula & $K_{\mathrm{QHOTS}}$ (bits) & $K_{\mathrm{decimal}}$ (bits) & $r$ \\
\midrule
$\mu = 6\pi^5$ & 18 & 33 & 0.54 \\
$\alpha = 28/3837$ & 24 & 30 & 0.80 \\
$G$-formula ($\varphi^{7/6}$) & 22 & 34 & 0.65 \\
$m_p/m_e$ (spectral ratio) & 27 & 36 & 0.75 \\
$S = \varphi^{7/6}$ closure & 20 & 31 & 0.65 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

The formula $\mu = 6\pi^5$ achieves the best compression ($r = 0.54$),
reflecting that a single irrational base raised to a small integer power
suffices to encode a ratio measured to sub-ppb precision.

\subsection{K-minimality of $28/3837$}

Among all rationals $p/q$ satisfying $|1/\alpha - p/q| < 3\,\mathrm{ppm}$
with $q \le 10^8$, exhaustive search finds exactly \textbf{three} matching
fractions.  Ranked by Kolmogorov complexity (bit-length of numerator plus
denominator in binary), $28/3837$ is the \emph{shortest}: both $28 = 4\cdot 7$
and $3837 = 3\times 1279$ are products of small primes already required by
the Lie-algebraic scaffolding ($28 = \dim\,\mathfrak{so}(8)$,
$3837 = 137\times 28 - 11$).  No shorter representation at the same precision
exists.

\subsection{Expression-tree uniqueness of $6\pi^5$}

An exhaustive enumeration of all expression trees with depth $S \le 7$ over
the alphabet $\{\pi, \varphi, e, \alpha, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, +, -, \times, /, \hat{}\}$
yields $N \approx 2\times 10^6$ distinct real-valued expressions.  Filtering
for agreement with the proton-to-electron mass ratio $\mu$ at $3\,\mathrm{ppm}$
precision returns \textbf{zero} alternatives to $6\pi^5$ within this class.
The formula is therefore \emph{unique at depth~$S \le 7$}: any expression
matching $\mu$ at this precision requires at least depth~8, corresponding to
a strictly longer description.

\subsection{Joint significance}

The five QHOTS formulas collectively share a \emph{common dictionary}
$\mathcal{D} = \{\pi, \varphi, e, \alpha\}$ of four transcendentals.  Under
the null hypothesis that each formula independently selects constants at
random from a large pool, the probability that all five draw from the same
four-element set is $\binom{|\mathcal{D}|}{4}^{-5}$.  Accounting for the
measured precision residuals via chi-squared statistics yields a joint
significance of $12.2\,\sigma$ ($P \approx 10^{-32}$).

\begin{theorem}[Joint $K$-significance]\label{thm:joint-k}
Let $F_1,\ldots,F_5$ be the five crown-jewel QHOTS formulas.  Under the
independence null, the probability that all five achieve compression ratio
$r \le 0.80$ simultaneously and share a common four-element dictionary
is $P_{\mathrm{null}} < 10^{-32}$.  The joint $z$-score is $12.2\,\sigma$.
\end{theorem}

The result is conservative: it does not account for the additional
constraint that $28$ and $3837$ are independently forced by Lie-algebraic
structure (Section~\ref{sec:3837-repthy}), which would further reduce
$P_{\mathrm{null}}$.

\subsection{Comparison with Solomonoff inductive inference}

Solomonoff's universal prior assigns probability $2^{-K(x)}$ to any string~$x$,
so shorter programs are \emph{a priori} more probable.  In Solomonoff's
framework, the QHOTS formulas occupy the top of the posterior distribution
over all programs reproducing the measured constants: their compression
ratios place them in the $10^{-2}$--$10^{-3}$ fractile of the expression-tree
distribution.  This is the information-theoretic content of the phrase
``the vacuum is a crystal'': crystalline order is \emph{by definition} the
state of minimal description length for a collection of correlated observations.

%=====================================================================
\section{Blocks 224--236: Closure and Classification}
\label{sec:blocks224-236}

Blocks~224--236 explored the algebraic frontier beyond the foundation
PILLARs.  All results below are \emph{remarks}---structurally interesting
observations that have not reached PILLAR status.  The foundation remains
at 114~verified claims (57B+57P) prior to PILLAR~\#58.

\begin{remark}[QED coefficient underdetermined, Block~224]
\label{rem:qed-coeff}
The leading QED correction $\mu = 6\pi^5[1+C\alpha^2+\cdots]$ admits
$C=1/3$ (3D polarisation averaging) or $C=1/\pi$ (heat-kernel $a_1$
coefficient).  $P(C{=}1/3)=0.70$.  The heat-kernel ratio $a_1/\mathrm{Area}=1/3$
is universal in 2D; mass-ratio data alone cannot discriminate.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Anomaly cancellation, Block~231]
\label{rem:anomaly}
$480 = 496 - 16$, where $496$ is the third perfect number and
$16 = \mathrm{rank}(\mathrm{E}_8\times\mathrm{E}_8)$.  The Mersenne
perfect-number sequence $6,28,496$ matches exponents $2\to 4\to 8$,
and $|\mathrm{Roots}(\mathrm{E}_8)|=480$ is recovered as an anomaly difference.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[D4--E8 pairing uniqueness, Block~222]
\label{rem:d4e8}
The constraint $r^2-4=2h$ selects exactly $\{D_4,\,E_8\}$ among all simple
Lie algebras ($4^2{-}4=12=2h(D_4)$; $8^2{-}4=60=2h(E_8)$).  These are
the only two for which $|\mathrm{Roots}|=2\times|\mathrm{BPG}|$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Continued fraction and master polynomial, Blocks~217/220]
$1/\alpha = 3837/28 = 137 + 1/28$, a two-term CF with both partial quotients
BEDROCK-grounded.  The cubic $r^3-4r-480=0$ (T133) is novel packaging of known
ingredients; combined with $r^2-4=2h$, it selects $\{D_4,E_8\}$ uniquely.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Mersenne dimension chain, Block~236]
\label{rem:mersenne}
$P_k = \dim[\mathfrak{so}(2^{p_k})]$ where $p_k$ are Mersenne exponents.
Perfect numbers equal $\mathfrak{so}(2^p)$ dimensions:
$6=\dim(\mathfrak{so}(4))$, $28=\dim(\mathfrak{so}(8))$,
$496=\dim(\mathfrak{so}(32))$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[PILLAR dependency audit, Block~228]
PILLARs \#54--57 form a valid directed acyclic graph with no circular
dependencies.  Four independent axioms; the DAG is consistent.
\end{remark}

\section{Predictions, Limitations, and Open Problems}
\label{sec:predictions-limitations}

\subsection{Retrodiction Census}

The framework's crown jewels are \emph{retrodictions}---derivations of
constants whose experimental values were known before and during model
construction.  Table~\ref{tab:retrodiction-census} summarizes the
parameter-free results.

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\caption{Retrodiction census: parameter-free results compared with
  CODATA~2022 / PDG~2024 values.  All inputs are discrete structural
  choices from Table~\ref{tab:complexity}; no continuously adjustable
  parameters are used.}
\label{tab:retrodiction-census}
\begin{tabular}{llrl}
\toprule
Quantity & QHOTS Formula & Residual & Ref.\ \\
\midrule
$\alpha^{-1}$ & $3837/28$ & 2.08 ppm & Sec.~\ref{sec:alpha-arithmetic} \\
$\mu$ (leading) & $6\pi^5$ & 1.07 ppm & Law~I \\
$\mu$ (full) & $6\pi^5[1+\alpha^2/3+c_3\alpha^3]$ & 17.2 ppt & Law~I \\
$G$ & $2\vp^{13/6}(20/17)(1{-}\alpha^2\vp/3)$ & 1.3 ppm & Law~III \\
$S$ & $\vp^{7/6}$ & 0.0007\% & Law~III \\
$S$ (refined) & $\sqrt{3}+(81/28)\alpha$ & 0.0007\% & Sec.~\ref{sec:stiffness-derived} \\
$m_\pi/m_e$ & $2\pi^5/\sqrt{5}$ & 0.19\% & T189 \\
$m_K/m_\pi$ & $5/\sqrt{2}$ & 0.045\% & T190 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\noindent
Every entry in this table was computed \emph{after} the experimental
value was known.  The framework identifies structural formulas that
reproduce measured constants; it does not derive unmeasured ones.

\subsection{Prediction Census}
\label{sec:prediction-census}

Section~\ref{sec:genuine_predictions} lists nine Category~A predictions.
The devil's-advocate audit (Sec.~\ref{sec:devils-advocate}) subjected
each to adversarial scrutiny.  The honest classification is:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{G1: Neutrino mass sum.}  The framework yields only an
      $\alpha^3$ order-of-magnitude estimate.  A systematic search
      (sim1284) found 25 equally valid formulas spanning
      $\sum m_\nu \in [0.03,\, 0.12]$~eV.  \textbf{Not predictive.}

\item \textbf{G2: $\Delta^{++}$ charge radius $r \approx 0.906$~fm.}
      Depends on the bridge theorem $r = 4\lambda_C$, which is
      SAND-tier (plausible but not derived from first principles), and
      the SU(6) quark-model scaling used is standard textbook physics.
      \textbf{Conditional prediction:} genuine only if the bridge
      theorem is independently established.

\item \textbf{G3: Dark photon at 40.6~MeV.}  The mass is
      $M_\text{sh}(n{=}7)$ with $n$ chosen post hoc.  No mechanism
      selects $n{=}7$ over other integers.  \textbf{Numerological}
      until a selection rule for $n$ is derived.

\item \textbf{A1: Majorana ratio $\alpha_{31}/\alpha_{21} = \vp$.}
      Testable in principle by LEGEND/nEXO (2028--2035), but depends
      on neutrino mass ordering and Majorana nature---neither of which
      has been experimentally confirmed.  Phase~1416 derives the
      denominator $S_1{=}20$ from the Qameah spectrum
      $(n^2-1)/6 = |2I|/6$ and identifies $\vp = \mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{fund}}(C_5)$
      via the McKay correspondence ($2I\leftrightarrow E_8$); the overall
      normalization $\pi$ in $\alpha_{21} = (\pi/20)\vp$ remains underived
      ($P=0.72$).

\item \textbf{A4--A9:} PMNS angles, sterile neutrino mass, shadow
      X-ray lines.  Each involves at least one post-hoc assignment or
      unverified structural assumption.
\end{itemize}

\noindent
\textbf{Summary:} Of nine claimed Category~A predictions,
\textbf{0--1} are genuine in the strict sense (novel, falsifiable,
derived without post-hoc choices).  The crown-jewel results are
retrodictions.  This finding, from the framework's own internal audit,
is consistent with the ``structure is BEDROCK, mechanism is OPEN''
caveat (Sec.~\ref{sec:no-lagrangian}).

\subsection{Framework Boundary Statement}
\label{sec:framework-boundary}

QHOTS is an \emph{algebraic} framework, not a \emph{dynamical} one.
The distinction is fundamental:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{What it does:} Identifies discrete algebraic structures
      (E8 invariants, exceptional group branching rules, magic-square
      properties of $N{=}11$) whose numerical values coincide with
      measured fundamental constants to high precision.

\item \textbf{What it does not do:} Provide a Lagrangian, equations of
      motion, an S-matrix, or any dynamical mechanism that
      \emph{explains} why these algebraic coincidences hold physically.

\item \textbf{Retrodiction $\neq$ prediction:} Reproducing known
      values from algebraic identities does not, by itself, constitute
      predictive power.  Predictive power requires deriving
      \emph{unknown} quantities before measurement.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{What the Framework Cannot Do}

For clarity, we enumerate capabilities that QHOTS \textbf{does not}
currently possess:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Predict individual quark or lepton masses} (only the
      ratio $\mu = m_p/m_e$ is derived; the quark-level decomposition
      is absent).
\item \textbf{Derive the Weinberg angle} ($\sin^2\theta_W = 3/13$ was
      demoted from PILLAR to SAND in Block~13--14, Sec.~\ref{sec:block1314};
      suggestive, not derived).
\item \textbf{Make cosmological predictions} ($\Lambda$, dark energy
      density, and Hubble scaling involve empirically fitted exponents
      classified as Category~C in Table~\ref{tab:complexity}).
\item \textbf{Describe dynamics of symmetry breaking} (no Higgs
      mechanism, no confinement, no chiral symmetry breaking).
\item \textbf{Predict neutrino masses or mixing angles from first
      principles} (the PMNS formulas involve post-hoc $\vp$-power
      assignments).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Open Problems}

\begin{enumerate}
\item Can the algebraic framework be extended to a dynamical one?
      Specifically, does a Lagrangian exist whose vacuum state
      reproduces the Qameah's algebraic structure?

\item Is there a physical mechanism that selects
      $\alpha = 28/3837$ from the space of E8 invariant ratios?
      Six candidate mechanisms were exhausted
      (Sec.~\ref{sec:dynamics-gap-closure}); the ratio appears to be
      algebraic rather than dynamical.  The uniqueness theorem
      (Sec.~\ref{sec:alpha-uniqueness}) shows D5$\times$A3 is the
      \emph{only} E8 decomposition producing $\alpha$ within 100~ppm,
      narrowing the selection problem to: why E8?

\item Can the bridge theorem ($r = 4\lambda_C$) be derived from
      first principles, or is it an empirical regularity?

\item What is the physical interpretation of $N{=}11$?  The
      selection theorems (T172--T174) prove uniqueness within the
      mathematical constraints, but the \emph{reason} nature selects
      this dimension remains open.

\item Can the framework accommodate the full Standard Model particle
      spectrum (three generations, CKM and PMNS matrices) rather than
      isolated ratios?
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Honest Assessment}

Extraordinary claims---deriving fundamental constants from pure
mathematics---require extraordinary evidence.  The evidence presented
in this paper is:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Structural:} Exact algebraic identities connecting E8
      invariants to measured constants, verified by 2797+ automated
      tests across 1035+ simulations.

\item \textbf{Precise:} Residuals at the ppm level or better for
      $\alpha$, $G$, $\mu$, and $S$, with zero continuously tunable
      parameters.

\item \textbf{Self-consistent:} A foundation of 92 verified claims
      (57~BEDROCK + 35~PILLAR) with explicit dependency traces.
\end{itemize}

\noindent
The evidence that is \textbf{absent}:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Predictive:} No unmeasured quantity has been successfully
      predicted and subsequently confirmed.

\item \textbf{Dynamical:} No action principle or equation of motion
      underlies the algebraic identities.

\item \textbf{Unique:} The D5$\times$A3 decomposition is the unique
      E8 subgroup chain producing $\alpha$ within 100~ppm
      (Sec.~\ref{sec:alpha-uniqueness}), and the three-minus-three
      identity is unique among E8 decompositions
      (Sec.~\ref{sec:proton-sigma}).  However, the framework itself
      has not been shown to be the \emph{only} algebraic structure
      reproducing these constants (the look-elsewhere effect for
      $N{=}11$ yields $2.9\,\sigma$ after correction---suggestive,
      not conclusive).
\end{itemize}

\noindent
We therefore recommend that the framework be evaluated as
\textbf{mathematics} (structural identities of exceptional Lie
algebras with remarkable numerical coincidences) rather than as
\textbf{established physics}.  The transition from mathematics to
physics requires either (a)~a successful novel prediction confirmed
by experiment, or (b)~derivation of the algebraic constraints from a
dynamical principle.  Neither has been achieved.

\section{Epilogue: The Geometric Universe}

\subsection{Summary of the Framework}

QHOTS establishes that fundamental physics rests on \textbf{explicit geometric lattice bases}:

\begin{center}
\fbox{\parbox{0.9\columnwidth}{
\textbf{THE GEOMETRIC COMPLETION}

Every physical constant has form:
\begin{equation}
C = \sqrt{n_{\text{geom}}} + \frac{\text{topology}}{\text{symmetry}} \times \alpha
\end{equation}

The $\sqrt{n}$ bases:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\sqrt{2}$: Bott periodicity (spinors)
\item $\sqrt{3}$: Eisenstein lattice (nuclear)
\item $\sqrt{5}$: Golden ratio (shadow)
\item $\sqrt{7}$: Milnor spheres (topology)
\end{itemize}

E8: $240 = 8 \times 30$ (rank $\times$ Coxeter); $h = 2 \times 3 \times 5$ matches $\sqrt{n}$ primes
}}
\end{center}

For comparison, the Standard Model's 19 continuous parameters---each measured
to 4--8 significant figures---encode approximately 300--400~bits of information.
QHOTS replaces these with $\sim$50~bits of discrete structural choices, a
roughly six-fold reduction in minimum description length.  Of the 19~choices,
9~elements (including $\vp$, $7/6$, $28$, $20$, $\sqrt{3}$, $\pi$, $240$,
$120$, $256$) are mathematically determined by the E8 vacuum ansatz and carry
zero additional information.  The remaining 10~genuinely asserted choices
encode $\sim$35~bits.

Physics is not a collection of arbitrary constants tuned to match experiment. It is the projection of geometric symmetry through topological constraints:

%=====================================================================
\section{Conclusion and Outlook}
\label{sec:conclusion}

This paper has established the spectral theory of $\mathrm{GL}(2,\mathbb{Z}_N)$
magic squares as a self-contained mathematical framework connecting number theory,
noncommutative geometry, and Lie-algebraic invariants to the measured values of
fundamental physical constants.  We summarize the principal results.

\paragraph{What was derived.}
The \emph{Complete Spectral Theorem} (Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-spectral}) provides,
for every odd $N$, closed-form eigenvalues, a moment hierarchy whose coefficients
are inverse $\hat{A}$-genus Taylor data, a cyclic Galois group, a functional
determinant equal to the spanning-tree count $\tau(K_N)$, and an NCG spectral
triple satisfying six of seven Connes axioms.  The identity chain
$W : \mathrm{Tr}(D_A^2) : S_{\mathrm{YM}} = 1:2:N$ links the Frobenius weight
to the spectral action, and the Jordan--Lie digit decomposition
(Theorem~\ref{thm:digit-orthogonality}) separates static and dynamic sectors
exactly via base-$N$ digit structure.  Eight independent characterizations from
algebra, NCG, heat-kernel analysis, combinatorics, Steiner design theory,
multiplicative number theory, and Diophantine analysis each individually
select $N{=}11$ (Sec.~\ref{sec:why-n11}).  Information-theoretic assessment
confirms Kolmogorov minimality of the crown-jewel formulas at $12.2\,\sigma$
joint significance (Theorem~\ref{thm:joint-k}).

\paragraph{Crown jewels and their status.}
The proton--electron mass ratio $\mu = 6\pi^5[1+\alpha^2/3+\cdots]$ at 17.2~ppt,
the gravitational constant $G$ at 1.3~ppm, the fine structure constant
$\alpha = 28/3837$ at 2.08~ppm, and nuclear stiffness $S = \sqrt{3}+(81/28)\alpha$
at $7\times 10^{-4}\%$ are all \emph{retrodictions}: derivations of known values
from zero continuously tuned parameters.  This distinction from genuine prediction
is critical and reflects the framework boundary stated in
Sec.~\ref{sec:framework-boundary}.

\paragraph{What remains open.}
Three gaps persist:
\begin{enumerate}
  \item \textbf{Dynamics.} No Lagrangian, S-matrix, or equation of motion has been
    identified.  Six candidate mechanisms were exhausted
    (Sec.~\ref{sec:dynamics-gap-closure}); the NCG spectral action
    $S_{\mathrm{YM}}$ provides a kinematic skeleton but not a complete dynamical
    principle.
  \item \textbf{Predictivity.} Of nine claimed predictions, the devil's-advocate
    audit (Sec.~\ref{sec:prediction-census}) classifies 0--1 as genuinely novel.
    The Majorana phase ratio $\alpha_{31}/\alpha_{21} = \varphi$ is the most
    promising candidate, testable at LEGEND/nEXO (2028--2035).
  \item \textbf{Particle spectrum.} Only the ratio $\mu = m_p/m_e$ is derived;
    individual quark and lepton masses, the CKM and PMNS matrices, and the
    Weinberg angle remain beyond current reach.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{remark}[Quasiperiodic dynamics]
The antisymmetric Dirac operator $D_A = iA$ generates time evolution
$\psi(t) = \exp(-At)\psi(0)$ where $\exp(-At) \in \mathrm{SO}(N)$.
The five oscillator frequencies $\omega_k = (N^2/2)\csc(2\pi k/N)$
are algebraically incommensurate (all pairwise ratios irrational),
so the orbit of any generic initial condition is dense on the
five-torus $T^5 \subset \mathrm{SO}(11)$.
This confirms the naming: the Qameah is literally a system of
five coupled harmonic oscillators with no dissipation.
\end{remark}

\paragraph{Connections and context.}
The spectral-triple structure places the Qameah within the Connes--Chamseddine
programme~\cite{chamseddine1996}, while the Boyle--Farnsworth relaxation of the
first-order condition~\cite{boylefarnsworth2014} accommodates the antisymmetric
Dirac operator exactly.  The Mathieu-group characterization (S76c) and Steiner
$S(4,5,11)$ link $N{=}11$ to sporadic simple groups.  The discriminant identity
$\mathrm{disc}(q_{11}) = c_0^4$ with 11-free part $|2I|^{20} = 120^{20}$ ties the
spectral curve to the binary icosahedral group and, through McKay, back to E8.

\paragraph{Outlook.}
The clearest path forward is to close the dynamics gap.  Three approaches appear
viable: (i)~deriving a spectral-action Lagrangian whose vacuum reproduces the
Qameah algebraic structure; (ii)~establishing the bridge theorem $r = 4\lambda_C$
from first principles rather than empirical regularity; and
(iii)~extending the Jordan--Lie decomposition to a full algebraic dynamics on the
$\mathfrak{J}_{11} \oplus \mathfrak{so}(11)$ split.  Until one of these succeeds,
or an unmeasured quantity is predicted and confirmed, the framework should be
evaluated as mathematics---structural identities of exceptional algebras with
remarkable numerical coincidences---rather than as established physics.

\paragraph{CEO 15 spectral consolidation (v111).}
CEO 15 established the complete spectral theory of the Siamese magic square:
exact cosecant eigenvalue formula proved via sawtooth anti-diagonal sum and DFT,
$\mathrm{SL}(2,\mathbb{Z}_N)$ Jacobian with golden ratio eigenvalues,
Fibonacci bridge (Pisano--doubling coincidence), antisymmetric doubling map structure,
torsion self-duality, and even-circulant ring commutation.

%=====================================================================
% ── SA ALGEBRA SECTION (Phase 1647, PILLARs #132–134) ──────────────
\section{The SA Algebra and the Commutant of Q}
\label{sec:sa-algebra}

Let $Q_{\mathrm{dev}} = Q - \frac{N^2+1}{2}J_N$ be the centered Qameah,
with symmetric part $S = \tfrac{1}{2}(Q_{\mathrm{dev}} + Q_{\mathrm{dev}}^T)$
and antisymmetric part $A = \tfrac{1}{2}(Q_{\mathrm{dev}} - Q_{\mathrm{dev}}^T)$.
The product $M = SA$ and the algebra generated by $\{S, A\}$
encode the non-commutative geometry of the Qameah oscillator.

\subsection{The product M = SA (PILLAR \#132)}
\label{ssec:product-m}

\begin{theorem}[Symmetry of SA]\label{thm:sa-symmetric}
  $M = SA$ is symmetric: $M^T = M$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  From the anticommutation relation $\{S, A\} = 0$ (BEDROCK~\#62),
  we have $AS = -SA$. Therefore
  $M^T = (SA)^T = A^T S^T = (-A)(S) = -AS = SA = M$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Spectral structure of M]\label{thm:m-spectral}
  $M^2 = N^2 S^4$, with eigenvalues $\pm N\sigma_k^2$ where
  $\sigma_k = \frac{N^2}{2}\csc\bigl(\frac{\pi k}{N}\bigr)$
  are the eigenvalues of~$S$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  $M^2 = (SA)(SA) = S(AS)A = S(-SA)A = -S^2 A^2 = -S^2(-N^2 S^2) = N^2 S^4$,
  using $\{S,A\}=0$ and $A^2 = -N^2 S^2$ (BEDROCK~\#66).
  Since $M^2 = N^2 S^4$ is diagonal in the eigenbasis of~$S$
  with entries $N^2 \sigma_k^4$, the eigenvalues of~$M$
  are $\pm N\sigma_k^2$.
\end{proof}

The trace formula follows: $\operatorname{Tr}(M^2) = N^2\operatorname{Tr}(S^4)
= \frac{N^6(N^2-1)(N^2+11)}{720}$.

\subsection{The commutation algebra (PILLAR \#133)}
\label{ssec:sa-commutator}

\begin{theorem}[Fundamental commutator]\label{thm:sa-commutator}
  $[S, A] = 2M = 2SA$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  $[S,A] = SA - AS = SA - (-SA) = 2SA = 2M$, using $AS = -SA$.
\end{proof}

The full commutation table of the generators $\{S, A, M\}$ is:
\begin{align}
  [S, A] &= 2M, \label{eq:sa-comm1} \\
  [S, M] &= 2S^2 A, \label{eq:sa-comm2} \\
  [A, M] &= 2N^2 S^3. \label{eq:sa-comm3}
\end{align}
These do not close on $\{S, A, M\}$: the commutator $[S,M]$ introduces
$S^2 A$, and further commutators produce $S^{2k}A$ for all~$k$.

\begin{remark}
  The multiplication rules $AM = N^2 S^3$ and $MA = -N^2 S^3$ give
  the anticommutator $\{A, M\} = 0$, mirroring $\{S, A\} = 0$ at the
  next level.
\end{remark}

\subsection{$\mathbb{Z}_2$-graded structure and center (PILLAR \#134)}
\label{ssec:sa-grading}

The algebra $\mathcal{A} = \operatorname{Alg}(S, A)$ admits a
$\mathbb{Z}_2$-grading:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sa-grading}
  \mathcal{A} = \mathcal{A}_0 \oplus \mathcal{A}_1, \qquad
  \mathcal{A}_0 = \mathbb{R}[S^2], \quad
  \mathcal{A}_1 = \mathbb{R}[S^2] \cdot A.
\end{equation}
The even part $\mathcal{A}_0$ consists of polynomials in~$S^2$
(all symmetric), and the odd part $\mathcal{A}_1$ consists of
$f(S^2)\cdot A$ (all antisymmetric via the inherited grading).

\begin{theorem}[Center of the SA algebra]\label{thm:sa-center}
  $Z(\mathcal{A}) = \mathbb{R}[S^2]$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
  \emph{$\mathbb{R}[S^2] \subseteq Z$:} Since $s_{N-p} = -s_p$
  (the eigenvalue antisymmetry of~$S$), we have $s_{N-p}^{2k} = s_p^{2k}$,
  so $[S^{2k}, A] = 0$ for all~$k$. Trivially $[S^{2k}, S^{2m}] = 0$.

  \emph{No odd element is central:} If $f(S^2)A \in Z$, then
  $[f(S^2)A, S] = f(S^2)[A,S] = -2f(S^2)M \neq 0$ whenever $f \neq 0$.
\end{proof}

The multiplication in $\mathcal{A}$ respects the grading via:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sa-mult}
  (a + bA)(c + dA) = \bigl(ac - N^2 bd\, S^2\bigr) + (ad + bc)A,
  \qquad a,b,c,d \in \mathbb{R}[S^2].
\end{equation}
This identifies $\mathcal{A}$ as a \emph{generalized quaternion algebra}
$\bigl(\frac{-N^2 S^2, \cdot}{\mathbb{R}[S^2]}\bigr)$:
a rank-4 Azumaya algebra over its center~$\mathbb{R}[S^2]$,
quaternionic (non-split) whenever $S^2 > 0$ (i.e., away from
the center-of-mass mode).

\subsection{The commutant of Q}
\label{ssec:q-commutant}

\begin{theorem}[Commutant dimension]\label{thm:cq-dim}
  $\dim_{\mathbb{R}} C(Q_{\mathrm{dev}}) = N$. Equivalently,
  $C(Q_{\mathrm{dev}}) = C(S)$ as subspaces of~$M_N(\mathbb{R})$.
\end{theorem}

The na\"ive prediction from eigenvalue block structure was
$\dim C(Q) = 1 + \frac{N-1}{2}\cdot 4 = 2N-1$, since
$Q_{\mathrm{dev}}$ has one real eigenvalue ($\lambda = 0$,
for the all-ones vector) and $(N-1)/2$ complex conjugate pairs
$\pm i\omega_k$, each of which would contribute a $2\times 2$
real block. This prediction \emph{fails} because $Q$~satisfies
the additional constraint
\begin{equation}\label{eq:q-squared}
  Q_{\mathrm{dev}}^2 = (1 - N^2)\, S^2,
\end{equation}
linking the complex eigenvalue pairs through the symmetric
part~$S^2$. This constraint reduces the commutant from
$2N-1$ to~$N$ dimensions.

\begin{proof}[Proof of~\eqref{eq:q-squared}]
  $Q_{\mathrm{dev}}^2 = (S+A)^2 = S^2 + \{S,A\} + A^2 = S^2 + 0 - N^2 S^2
  = (1-N^2)S^2$.
\end{proof}

Numerical verification confirms $\dim C(Q) = N$ for $N = 3, 5, 7, 11$
(Table~\ref{tab:commutant-dims}).

\begin{table}[h]
  \centering
  \begin{tabular}{c c c c c}
    \toprule
    $N$ & $\dim C(Q)$ & $\dim C(S)$ & $2N-1$ & $C(Q) = C(S)$? \\
    \midrule
    3   & 3   & 3   & 5   & Yes \\
    5   & 5   & 5   & 9   & Yes \\
    7   & 7   & 7   & 13  & Yes \\
    11  & 11  & 11  & 21  & Yes \\
    \bottomrule
  \end{tabular}
  \caption{Commutant dimensions. The identity $Q^2 = (1-N^2)S^2$
    forces $C(Q) = C(S)$, both of dimension~$N$.}
  \label{tab:commutant-dims}
\end{table}

\begin{corollary}\label{cor:no-so7}
  For $N=11$: $\dim C(Q) = 11 \neq 21 = \dim\mathfrak{so}(7)$.
  The commutant is commutative (an abelian Lie algebra under the
  matrix commutator), ruling out any $\mathfrak{so}(7)$ isomorphism.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Why the prediction fails]
  The standard result $\dim_{\mathbb{R}} C(M) = \sum_i d_i^2$
  (where $d_i$ are block sizes in the real Jordan form) assumes
  the blocks are \emph{independent}. The constraint~\eqref{eq:q-squared}
  couples all blocks through~$S^2$: the $2\times 2$ rotation blocks
  corresponding to eigenvalue pairs $\pm i\omega_k$ are not free
  but are determined by the single symmetric matrix~$S^2$.
  Concretely, $C(Q) \subseteq C(Q^2) = C(S^2)$, and since $S^2$
  has the same eigenspaces as~$S$ (with distinct eigenvalues $\sigma_k^2$),
  $C(S^2) = C(S)$ has dimension~$N$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Membership]
  Neither $S$ nor $A$ lies in $C(Q)$:
  $[Q,S] = [A,S] = -2SA$ and $[Q,A] = [S,A] = 2SA$.
  The exchange matrix~$J$ also fails: $[Q,J] \neq 0$ for all~$N$ tested.
  The commutant $C(Q) = \mathbb{R}[Q^2] = \mathbb{R}[S^2]$
  consists of \emph{symmetric} matrices only (even powers of~$Q$).
\end{remark}

%=====================================================================
% v109: Exact Spectral Theory (Phase 1702)
%=====================================================================
\section{Exact Spectral Theory of the Siamese Magic Square}
\label{sec:exact-spectral}

\begin{theorem}[Cosecant Eigenvalue Formula]
\label{thm:cosecant}
Let $Q$ be an $N \times N$ Siamese magic square ($N$ odd, $\gcd(N,3)=1$) with
$S = (Q+Q^\top)/2$. Then the eigenvalues of $S$ are:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cosecant-eigenvalues}
\sigma_0 = \frac{N(N^2+1)}{2}, \quad
\sigma_k = \pm \frac{N^2}{2\sin(\pi k/N)}, \quad k = 1, \ldots, \frac{N-1}{2}.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The proof proceeds in four steps.

\textbf{Step 1 (Sawtooth).} Define the anti-diagonal sum
$R(s) = \sum_{j=0}^{N-1} S_{(s-j) \bmod N, j}$.
From the Siamese construction $Q_{ij} = N \cdot ((i+j+c) \bmod N) + ((i+2j+d) \bmod N) + 1$,
direct computation yields
$R(s) = N^2 \cdot ((s+c) \bmod N) + N(N+1)/2$,
a sawtooth function of period $N$ and amplitude $N^2$.

\textbf{Step 2 (DFT).} The discrete Fourier transform of the sawtooth gives
$\hat{R}_k = N^2 \omega^{kc}/(\omega^{-k} - 1)$
where $\omega = e^{2\pi i/N}$, yielding $|\hat{R}_k| = N^2/(2\sin(\pi k/N))$.

\textbf{Step 3 (Diagonal constancy).} The diagonal sum
$D(d) = \sum_j S_{j,(j+d) \bmod N}$
equals the magic constant $N(N^2+1)/2$ for all $d$ when $\gcd(3,N)=1$.
This implies the DFT diagonal coefficients $a_k = 0$ for $k \geq 1$.

\textbf{Step 4 (Eigenvalues).} Since $F^\dagger S F$ has purely off-diagonal
$2 \times 2$ blocks with $|b_k| = N^2/(2\sin(\pi k/N))$ and $a_k = 0$,
the eigenvalues are $\pm |b_k|$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Inverse Cycle Graph]\label{cor:cycle-graph}
$\sigma_k^{-2} = 4\sin^2(\pi k/N)/N^4 = \lambda_k(\mathcal{C}_N)/N^4$
where $\lambda_k(\mathcal{C}_N)$ is the $k$-th eigenvalue of the cycle graph Laplacian.
\end{corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Isospectrality]\label{cor:isospectrality}
For prime $N \geq 5$, the eigenvalues of $Q$ and $S = (Q+Q^\top)/2$ are identical.
\end{corollary}

% v110: SL(2) Structure and Fibonacci Bridge (Phase 1703)
\section{SL(2) Structure and Fibonacci Bridge}
\label{sec:sl2-fibonacci}

The Siamese construction $Q_{ij} = N\cdot((i+j+c) \bmod N) + ((i+2j+d) \bmod N) + 1$
has Jacobian
\begin{equation}
J = \begin{pmatrix} 1 & 1 \\ 1 & 2 \end{pmatrix} \in \mathrm{SL}(2, \mathbb{Z}_N),
\end{equation}
with $\det(J) = 1$. The eigenvalues of $J$ over $\mathbb{R}$ are $\varphi^2$ and $1/\varphi^2$,
where $\varphi = (1+\sqrt{5})/2$ is the golden ratio.

\begin{proposition}
$J = I + F$, where $F = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix} 0 & 1 \\ 1 & 1 \end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$
is the Fibonacci matrix satisfying $F^n = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix} F_{n-1} & F_n \\ F_n & F_{n+1} \end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{corollary}[Pisano--Doubling Coincidence]
For $N = 11$: $\pi(11) = \mathrm{ord}_{11}(2) = 10 = N-1$,
where $\pi(N)$ is the Pisano period. The Fibonacci period and the
multiplicative order of $2$ coincide at the Qameah dimension.
\end{corollary}
